       defended the derivation of his equipartition theorem as correct, but suggested that gases might not be in
       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_equilibrium" title="Thermal equilibrium">
        thermal equilibrium
       </a>
       because of their interactions with the
       <a href="/wiki/Luminiferous_aether" title="Luminiferous aether">
        aether
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         [27]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/William_Thomson,_1st_Baron_Kelvin" title="William Thomson, 1st Baron Kelvin">
        Lord Kelvin
       </a>
       suggested that the derivation of the equipartition theorem must be incorrect, since it disagreed with experiment, but was unable to show how.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 1900
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_Strutt,_3rd_Baron_Rayleigh" title="John Strutt, 3rd Baron Rayleigh">
        Lord Rayleigh
       </a>
       instead put forward a more radical view that the equipartition theorem and the experimental assumption of thermal equilibrium were
       <i>
        both
       </i>
       correct; to reconcile them, he noted the need for a new principle that would provide an "escape from the destructive simplicity" of the equipartition theorem.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         [29]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">
        Albert Einstein
       </a>
       provided that escape, by showing in 1906 that these anomalies in the specific heat were due to quantum effects, specifically the quantization of energy in the elastic modes of the solid.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         [30]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Einstein used the failure of equipartition to argue for the need of a new quantum theory of matter.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pais_1982_11-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-pais_1982-11">
         [11]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <a href="/wiki/Walther_Nernst" title="Walther Nernst">
        Nernst's
       </a>
       1910 measurements of specific heats at low temperatures
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         [31]
        </a>
       </sup>
       supported Einstein's theory, and led to the widespread acceptance of
       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">
        quantum theory
       </a>
       among physicists.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         [32]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="General_formulation_of_the_equipartition_theorem">
        General formulation of the equipartition theorem
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: General formulation of the equipartition theorem">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Generalized_coordinates" title="Generalized coordinates">
        Generalized coordinates
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Hamiltonian_mechanics" title="Hamiltonian mechanics">
        Hamiltonian mechanics
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Microcanonical_ensemble" title="Microcanonical ensemble">
        Microcanonical ensemble
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_ensemble" title="Canonical ensemble">
        Canonical ensemble
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The most general form of the equipartition theorem states that under suitable assumptions (discussed below), for a physical system with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamiltonian_function" title="Hamiltonian function">
        Hamiltonian
       </a>
       energy function
       <i>
        H
       </i>
       and degrees of freedom
       <i>
        x
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
       </i>
       , the following equipartition formula holds in thermal equilibrium for all indices
       <i>
        m
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       :
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huang_1987_9-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-huang_1987-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tolman_1918_12-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-tolman_1918-12">
         [12]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \!{\Bigl \langle }x_{m}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=\delta _{mn}k_{B}T.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                x
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  H
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   x
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    n
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                δ
                <!-- δ -->
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 B
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \!{\Bigl \langle }x_{m}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=\delta _{mn}k_{B}T.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\!{\Bigl \langle }x_{{m}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial x_{{n}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=\delta _{{mn}}k_{{B}}T." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0b1c9a34cb24cb7b2eaaf9c7336631be2a60ec47" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; margin-left: -0.387ex; width:22.314ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Here
       <i>
        δ
        <sub>
         mn
        </sub>
       </i>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Kronecker_delta" title="Kronecker delta">
        Kronecker delta
       </a>
       , which is equal to one if
       <i>
        m
       </i>
       =
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       and is zero otherwise. The averaging brackets
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \left\langle \ldots \right\rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mrow>
              <mo>
               ⟨
              </mo>
              <mo>
               …
               <!-- … -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               ⟩
              </mo>
             </mrow>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \left\langle \ldots \right\rangle }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\left\langle \ldots \right\rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/977d09845a19bebb1af784016a4008a2ef3f5e88" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.533ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
       </span>
       is assumed to be an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ensemble_average" title="Ensemble average">
        ensemble average
       </a>
       over phase space or, under an assumption of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ergodic" title="Ergodic">
        ergodicity
       </a>
       , a time average of a single system.
      </p>
      <p>
       The general equipartition theorem holds in both the
       <a href="/wiki/Microcanonical_ensemble" title="Microcanonical ensemble">
        microcanonical ensemble
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huang_1987_9-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-huang_1987-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       when the total energy of the system is constant, and also in the
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_ensemble" title="Canonical ensemble">
        canonical ensemble
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tolman_1938_33-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tolman_1938-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       when the system is coupled to a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heat_bath" title="Heat bath">
        heat bath
       </a>
       with which it can exchange energy. Derivations of the general formula are given
       <a href="#Derivations">
        later in the article
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The general formula is equivalent to the following two:
      </p>
      <ol>
       <li>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }x_{n}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=k_{B}T\quad {\mbox{for all }}n}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                x
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  H
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   x
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    n
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 B
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mspace width="1em">
              </mspace>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
                <mtext>
                 for all
                </mtext>
               </mstyle>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               n
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }x_{n}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=k_{B}T\quad {\mbox{for all }}n}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\Bigl \langle }x_{{n}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial x_{{n}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=k_{{B}}T\quad {\mbox{for all }}n" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d48cf68c7c33fb1e47a3fd1f3a07fffb65354837" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:27.637ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </li>
       <li>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }x_{m}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=0\quad {\mbox{for all }}m\neq n.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                x
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mi>

                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   x
                  </mi>

                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               0
              </mn>
              <mspace width="1em">
              </mspace>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
                <mtext>
                 for all
                </mtext>
               </mstyle>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               m
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ≠
               <!-- ≠ -->
              </mo>
              <mi>

              </mi>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }x_{m}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=0\quad {\mbox{for all }}m\neq n.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\Bigl \langle }x_{{m}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial x_{{n}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=0\quad {\mbox{for all }}m\neq n." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/ec705f6ea33dfe1cee00b1ef0a7072a92e23c1ca" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:30.715ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </li>
      </ol>
      <p>
       If a degree of freedom
       <i>
        x
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
       </i>
       appears only as a quadratic term
       <i>
        a
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
        x
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
       </i>
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       in the Hamiltonian
       <i>
        H
       </i>
       , then the first of these formulae implies that
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle k_{B}T={\Bigl \langle }x_{n}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=2\langle a_{n}x_{n}^{2}\rangle ,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 B
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                x
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  H
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   x
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    n
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               2
              </mn>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟨
               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                a
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <msubsup>
               <mi>
                x
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msubsup>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟩
               <!-- ⟩ -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle k_{B}T={\Bigl \langle }x_{n}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=2\langle a_{n}x_{n}^{2}\rangle ,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="k_{{B}}T={\Bigl \langle }x_{{n}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial x_{{n}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=2\langle a_{n}x_{n}^{2}\rangle ," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8002e8910bc55ef1ff16ec7150ea07bb74b22dc6" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:29.23ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       which is twice the contribution that this degree of freedom makes to the average energy
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \langle H\rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              ⟨
              <!-- ⟨ -->
             </mo>
             <mi>
              H
             </mi>
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              ⟩
              <!-- ⟩ -->
             </mo>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \langle H\rangle }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\langle H\rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/20097765034f46c439c5cc029e8971db1662e5bf" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:3.873ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
       </span>
       . Thus the equipartition theorem for systems with quadratic energies follows easily from the general formula. A similar argument, with 2 replaced by
       <i>
        s
       </i>
       , applies to energies of the form
       <i>
        a
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
        x
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
        <sup>
         s
        </sup>
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       The degrees of freedom
       <i>
        x
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
       </i>
       are coordinates on the
       <a href="/wiki/Phase_space" title="Phase space">
        phase space
       </a>
       of the system and are therefore commonly subdivided into
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_coordinates" title="Canonical coordinates">
        generalized position
       </a>
       coordinates
       <i>
        q
        <sub>
         k
        </sub>
       </i>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Generalized_momentum" title="Generalized momentum">
        generalized momentum
       </a>
       coordinates
       <i>
        p
        <sub>
         k
        </sub>
       </i>
       , where
       <i>
        p
        <sub>
         k
        </sub>
       </i>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conjugate_momentum" title="Conjugate momentum">
        conjugate momentum
       </a>
       to
       <i>
        q
        <sub>
         k
        </sub>
       </i>
       . In this situation, formula 1 means that for all
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       ,
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }p_{k}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial p_{k}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\Bigl \langle }q_{k}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial q_{k}}}{\Bigr \rangle }=k_{\rm {B}}T.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 k
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  H
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   p
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    k
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 k
                </mi>
               </mrow>

      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Relation_to_the_virial_theorem">
        Relation to the virial theorem
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Relation to the virial theorem">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_theorem" title="Virial theorem">
        Virial theorem
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Generalized_coordinates" title="Generalized coordinates">
        Generalized coordinates
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Hamiltonian_mechanics" title="Hamiltonian mechanics">
        Hamiltonian mechanics
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The general equipartition theorem is an extension of the
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_theorem" title="Virial theorem">
        virial theorem
       </a>
       (proposed in 1870
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       ), which states that
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}q_{k}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial q_{k}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}p_{k}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial p_{k}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}p_{k}{\frac {dq_{k}}{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle }=-{\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}q_{k}{\frac {dp_{k}}{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle },}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">

                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>

               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   p
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    k
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}q_{k}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial q_{k}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}p_{k}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial p_{k}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}p_{k}{\frac {dq_{k}}{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle }=-{\Bigl \langle }\sum _{k}q_{k}{\frac {dp_{k}}{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle },}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\Bigl \langle }\sum _{{k}}q_{{k}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial q_{{k}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\Bigl \langle }\sum _{{k}}p_{{k}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial p_{{k}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\Bigl \langle }\sum _{{k}}p_{{k}}{\frac  {dq_{{k}}}{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle }=-{\Bigl \langle }\sum _{{k}}q_{{k}}{\frac  {dp_{{k}}}{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle }," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/faf4ea915406b58c4e082018cf6880c0e4d4bc0e" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:65.577ex; height:6.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <i>
        t
       </i>
       denotes
       <a href="/wiki/Time" title="Time">
        time
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-goldstein_1980_8-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-goldstein_1980-8">
         [8]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Two key differences are that the virial theorem relates
       <i>
        summed
       </i>
       rather than
       <i>
        individual
       </i>
       averages to each other, and it does not connect them to the
       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">
        temperature
       </a>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       . Another difference is that traditional derivations of the virial theorem use averages over time, whereas those of the equipartition theorem use averages over
       <a href="/wiki/Phase_space" title="Phase space">
        phase space
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">
        Applications
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Applications">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Ideal_gas_law">
        Ideal gas law
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Ideal gas law">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">
        Ideal gas
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
        Ideal gas law
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">
        Ideal gases
       </a>
       provide an important application of the equipartition theorem. As well as providing the formula

         <img alt="{\begin{aligned}\langle H^{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}\rangle &amp;={\frac  {1}{2m}}\langle p_{{x}}^{{2}}+p_{{y}}^{{2}}+p_{{z}}^{{2}}\rangle \\&amp;={\frac  {1}{2}}{\biggl (}{\Bigl \langle }p_{{x}}{\frac  {\partial H^{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}}{\partial p_{{x}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }+{\Bigl \langle }p_{{y}}{\frac  {\partial H^{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}}{\partial p_{{y}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }+{\Bigl \langle }p_{{z}}{\frac  {\partial H^{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}}{\partial p_{{z}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }{\biggr )}={\frac  {3}{2}}k_{{B}}T\end{aligned}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/faa95152f476eee3831d9c91613369e9fd4eebb4" style="vertical-align: -5.338ex; width:66.2ex; height:11.843ex;"/>
        </span>

      <p>
       for the average kinetic energy per particle, the equipartition theorem can be used to derive the
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
        ideal gas law
       </a>
       from classical mechanics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       If
       <b>
        q
       </b>
       = (
       <i>
        q
        <sub>
         x
        </sub>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        q
        <sub>
         y
        </sub>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        q
        <sub>
         z
        </sub>
       </i>
       ) and
       <b>
        p
       </b>
       = (
       <i>
        p
        <sub>
         x
        </sub>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        p
        <sub>
         y
        </sub>
       </i>
       ,
       <i>
        p
        <sub>
         z
        </sub>
       </i>
       ) denote the position vector and momentum of a particle in the gas, and
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       is the net force on that particle, then
      </p>

       <i>

      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Translational_motion.gif">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="263" data-file-width="300" height="263" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/6/6d/Translational_motion.gif" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         Figure 5. The kinetic energy of a particular molecule can
         <a href="/wiki/Thermal_fluctuations" title="Thermal fluctuations">
          fluctuate wildly
         </a>
         , but the equipartition theorem allows its
         <i>
          average
         </i>
         energy to be calculated at any temperature. Equipartition also provides a derivation of the
         <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
          ideal gas law
         </a>
         , an equation that relates the
         <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">
          pressure
         </a>
         ,
         <a href="/wiki/Volume" title="Volume">
          volume
         </a>
         and
         <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">
          temperature
         </a>
         of the gas. (In this diagram five of the molecules have been colored red to track their motion; this coloration has no other significance.)
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       By
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newton%27s_third_law" title="Newton's third law">
        Newton's third law
       </a>
       and the ideal gas assumption, the net force on the system is the force applied by the walls of their container, and this force is given by the pressure
       <i>
        P
       </i>
       of the gas. Hence
      </p>

              </mn>
              <mi>
               P
              </mi>
              <mi>
               V
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle P\oint _{\mathrm {surface} }\mathbf {q} \cdot \mathbf {dS} =P\int _{\mathrm {volume} }\left({\boldsymbol {\nabla }}\cdot \mathbf {q} \right)\,dV=3PV,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="P\oint _{{{\mathrm  {surface}}}}{\mathbf  {q}}\cdot {\mathbf  {dS}}=P\int _{{{\mathrm  {volume}}}}\left({\boldsymbol  \nabla }\cdot {\mathbf  {q}}\right)\,dV=3PV," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/23a7c0289eb6c3229b42fcc618f0452ea1bc9bf3" style="vertical-align: -2.505ex; width:49.278ex; height:6.009ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where d
       <i>
        V
       </i>
       is an infinitesimal volume within the container and
       <i>
        V
       </i>
       is the total volume of the container.
      </p>
      <p>
       Putting these equalities together yields
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle 3Nk_{B}T=-{\biggl \langle }\sum _{k=1}^{N}\mathbf {q} _{k}\cdot \mathbf {F} _{k}{\biggr \rangle }=3PV,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mn>
               3
              </mn>
              <mi>
               N
              </mi>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 B
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="2.047em" minsize="2.047em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <munderover>
               <mo>
                ∑
                <!-- ∑ -->
               </mo>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 k
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 =
                </mo>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 N
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </munderover>
              <msub>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="bold">
                 q
                </mi>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 k
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="bold">
                 F
                </mi>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 k
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="2.047em" minsize="2.047em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               3
              </mn>
              <mi>
               P
              </mi>
              <mi>
               V
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle 3Nk_{B}T=-{\biggl \langle }\sum _{k=1}^{N}\mathbf {q} _{k}\cdot \mathbf {F} _{k}{\biggr \rangle }=3PV,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="3Nk_{B}T=-{\biggl \langle }\sum _{k=1}^{N}\mathbf {q} _{k}\cdot \mathbf {F} _{k}{\biggr \rangle }=3PV," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/de090eb7113752f7651245314d1e2d7dc203b572" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:35.466ex; height:7.343ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       which immediately implies the
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
        ideal gas law
       </a>
       for
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       particles:
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle PV=Nk_{B}T=nRT,\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               P
              </mi>
              <mi>
               V
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               N
              </mi>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 B
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               n
              </mi>
              <mi>
               R
              </mi>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle PV=Nk_{B}T=nRT,\,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="PV=Nk_{B}T=nRT,\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/0cf740e4ec276f28f8bfe7685b8d0e20ddcce8e2" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:21.949ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       =
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       <sub>
        A
       </sub>
       is the number of moles of gas and
       <i>
        R
       </i>
       =
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       <sub>
        A
       </sub>
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       is the
       <a href="/wiki/Gas_constant" title="Gas constant">
        gas constant
       </a>
       . Although equipartition provides a simple derivation of the ideal-gas law and the internal energy, the same results can be obtained by an alternative method using the
       <a href="/wiki/Partition_function_(statistical_mechanics)" title="Partition function (statistical mechanics)">
        partition function
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-configint_35-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-configint-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diatomic_gases">
        Diatomic gases
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Diatomic gases">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Two-body_problem" title="Two-body problem">
        Two-body problem
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Rigid_rotor" title="Rigid rotor">
        Rigid rotor
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Harmonic_oscillator" title="Harmonic oscillator">
        Harmonic oscillator
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       A diatomic gas can be modelled as two masses,
       <i>
        m
       </i>
       <sub>
        1
       </sub>
       and
       <i>
        m
       </i>
       <sub>
        2
       </sub>
       , joined by a
       <a href="/wiki/Spring_(device)" title="Spring (device)">
        spring
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Hooke%27s_law" title="Hooke's law">
        stiffness
       </a>
       <i>
        a
       </i>
       , which is called the
       <i>
        rigid rotor-harmonic oscillator approximation
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcquarrie_2000c_19-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mcquarrie_2000c-19">
         [19]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The classical energy of this system is
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle H={\frac {\left|\mathbf {p} _{1}\right|^{2}}{2m_{1}}}+{\frac {\left|\mathbf {p} _{2}\right|^{2}}{2m_{2}}}+{\frac {1}{2}}aq^{2},}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               H
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <msup>
                 <mrow>
                  <mo>
                   |
                  </mo>
                  <msub>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mi mathvariant="bold">
                     p
                    </mi>
                   </mrow>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     1
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <mo>
                   |
                  </mo>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msup>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  2
                 </mn>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   m
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mn>
                    1
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <msup>
                 <mrow>
                  <mo>
                   |
                  </mo>
                  <msub>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mi mathvariant="bold">
                     p
                    </mi>
                   </mrow>
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mn>
                     2
                    </mn>
                   </mrow>
                  </msub>
                  <mo>
                   |
                  </mo>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msup>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  2
                 </mn>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   m
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mn>
                    2
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               a
              </mi>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle H={\frac {\left|\mathbf {p} _{1}\right|^{2}}{2m_{1}}}+{\frac {\left|\mathbf {p} _{2}\right|^{2}}{2m_{2}}}+{\frac {1}{2}}aq^{2},}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="H={\frac  {\left|{\mathbf  {p}}_{{1}}\right|^{{2}}}{2m_{{1}}}}+{\frac  {\left|{\mathbf  {p}}_{{2}}\right|^{{2}}}{2m_{{2}}}}+{\frac  {1}{2}}aq^{{2}}," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a11e702ce3b4d7792549399685a8da6f644f5a96" style="vertical-align: -2.171ex; width:28.299ex; height:6.343ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <b>
        p
       </b>
       <sub>
        1
       </sub>
       and
       <b>
        p
       </b>
       <sub>
        2
       </sub>
       are the momenta of the two atoms, and
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       is the deviation of the inter-atomic separation from its equilibrium value. Every degree of freedom in the energy is quadratic and, thus, should contribute ​
       <span class="frac nowrap">
        <sup>
         1
        </sup>
        ⁄
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
       </span>
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       to the total average energy, and ​
       <span class="frac nowrap">
        <sup>
         1
        </sup>
        ⁄
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
       </span>
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       to the heat capacity. Therefore, the heat capacity of a gas of
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       diatomic molecules is predicted to be 7
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       ·​
       <span class="frac nowrap">
        <sup>
         1
        </sup>
        ⁄
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
       </span>
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       : the momenta
       <b>
        p
       </b>
       <sub>
        1
       </sub>
       and
       <b>
        p
       </b>
       <sub>
        2
       </sub>
       contribute three degrees of freedom each, and the extension
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       contributes the seventh. It follows that the heat capacity of a mole of diatomic molecules with no other degrees of freedom should be (7/2)
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       <sub>
        A
       </sub>
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       = (7/2)
       <i>
        R
       </i>
       and, thus, the predicted molar heat capacity should be roughly 7 cal/(mol·K). However, the experimental values for molar heat capacities of diatomic gases are typically about 5 cal/(mol·K)
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Wueller_1896_23-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Wueller_1896-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and fall to 3 cal/(mol·K) at very low temperatures.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Eucken_1912_24-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Eucken_1912-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This disagreement between the equipartition prediction and the experimental value of the molar heat capacity cannot be explained by using a more complex model of the molecule, since adding more degrees of freedom can only
       <i>
        increase
       </i>
       the predicted specific heat, not decrease it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-maxwell_1875_25-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-maxwell_1875-25">
         [25]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This discrepancy was a key piece of evidence showing the need for a
       <a href="/wiki/Quantum_mechanics" title="Quantum mechanics">
        quantum theory
       </a>
       of matter.
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Chandra-crab.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2400" data-file-width="2400" height="300" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Chandra-crab.jpg/300px-Chandra-crab.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Chandra-crab.jpg/450px-Chandra-crab.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Chandra-crab.jpg/600px-Chandra-crab.jpg 2x" width="300"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Chandra-crab.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Figure 6. A combined X-ray and optical image of the
         <a href="/wiki/Crab_Nebula" title="Crab Nebula">
          Crab Nebula
         </a>
         . At the heart of this nebula there is a rapidly rotating
         <a href="/wiki/Neutron_star" title="Neutron star">
          neutron star
         </a>
         which has about one and a half times the mass of the
         <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">
          Sun
         </a>
         but is only 25 km across. The equipartition theorem is useful in predicting the properties of such neutron stars.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Extreme_relativistic_ideal_gases">
        Extreme relativistic ideal gases
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Extreme relativistic ideal gases">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">
        Special relativity
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/White_dwarf" title="White dwarf">
        White dwarf
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Neutron_star" title="Neutron star">
        Neutron star
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       Equipartition was used above to derive the classical
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas_law" title="Ideal gas law">
        ideal gas law
       </a>
       from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Newtonian_mechanics" title="Newtonian mechanics">
        Newtonian mechanics
       </a>
       . However,
       <a href="/wiki/Special_relativity" title="Special relativity">
        relativistic effects
       </a>
       become dominant in some systems, such as
       <a href="/wiki/White_dwarf" title="White dwarf">
        white dwarfs
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Neutron_star" title="Neutron star">
        neutron stars
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huang_1987_9-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-huang_1987-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the ideal gas equations must be modified. The equipartition theorem provides a convenient way to derive the corresponding laws for an extreme relativistic
       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">
        ideal gas
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In such cases, the kinetic energy of a
       <a href="/wiki/Relativistic_particle" title="Relativistic particle">
        single particle
       </a>
       is given by the formula
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {kin} }\approx cp=c{\sqrt {p_{x}^{2}+p_{y}^{2}+p_{z}^{2}}}.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                H
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  k
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  i
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  n
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               ≈
               <!-- ≈ -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
              <mi>
               p
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               c
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <msqrt>
                <msubsup>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   x
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msubsup>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <msubsup>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   y
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msubsup>
                <mo>
                 +
                </mo>
                <msubsup>
                 <mi>
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi>
                   z
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mn>
                   2
                  </mn>
                 </mrow>
                </msubsup>
               </msqrt>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {kin} }\approx cp=c{\sqrt {p_{x}^{2}+p_{y}^{2}+p_{z}^{2}}}.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="H_{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}\approx cp=c{\sqrt  {p_{{x}}^{{2}}+p_{{y}}^{{2}}+p_{{z}}^{{2}}}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/94bbb9b2737858292c6950fb12d152e2b07b6b84" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:29.223ex; height:4.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Taking the derivative of
       <i>
        H
       </i>
       with respect to the
       <i>
        p
        <sub>
         x
        </sub>
       </i>
       momentum component gives the formula
      </p>

         <img alt="{\begin{aligned}\langle H_{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}\rangle &amp;={\biggl \langle }c{\frac  {p_{{x}}^{{2}}+p_{{y}}^{{2}}+p_{{z}}^{{2}}}{{\sqrt  {p_{{x}}^{{2}}+p_{{y}}^{{2}}+p_{{z}}^{{2}}}}}}{\biggr \rangle }\\&amp;={\Bigl \langle }p_{{x}}{\frac  {\partial H^{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}}{\partial p_{{x}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }+{\Bigl \langle }p_{{y}}{\frac  {\partial H^{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}}{\partial p_{{y}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }+{\Bigl \langle }p_{{z}}{\frac  {\partial H^{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}}{\partial p_{{z}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }\\&amp;=3k_{{B}}T\end{aligned}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/38717fa994532838b47f2158e526d8ccbd8d2eab" style="vertical-align: -8.505ex; width:51.184ex; height:18.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where the last equality follows from the equipartition formula. Thus, the average total energy of an extreme relativistic gas is twice that of the non-relativistic case: for
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       particles, it is 3
       <i>
        Nk
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       .
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Non-ideal_gases">
        Non-ideal gases
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Non-ideal gases">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_expansion" title="Virial expansion">
        Virial expansion
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_coefficient" title="Virial coefficient">
        Virial coefficient
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       In an ideal gas the particles are assumed to interact only through collisions. The equipartition theorem may also be used to derive the energy and pressure of "non-ideal gases" in which the particles also interact with one another through
       <a href="/wiki/Conservative_force" title="Conservative force">
        conservative forces
       </a>
       whose potential
       <i>
        U
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        r
       </i>
       ) depends only on the distance
       <i>
        r
       </i>
       between the particles.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This situation can be described by first restricting attention to a single gas particle, and approximating the rest of the gas by a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Spherical_symmetry" title="Spherical symmetry">
        spherically symmetric
       </a>
       distribution. It is then customary to introduce a
       <a href="/wiki/Radial_distribution_function" title="Radial distribution function">
        radial distribution function
       </a>
       <i>
        g
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        r
       </i>
       ) such that the
       <a href="/wiki/Probability_density_function" title="Probability density function">
        probability density
       </a>
       of finding another particle at a distance
       <i>
        r
       </i>
       from the given particle is equal to 4π
       <i>
        r
       </i>
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       <i>
        ρg
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        r
       </i>
       ), where
       <i>
        ρ
       </i>
       =
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        V
       </i>
       is the mean
       <a href="/wiki/Density" title="Density">
        density
       </a>
       of the gas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcquarrie_2000b_36-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mcquarrie_2000b-36">
         [36]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It follows that the mean potential energy associated to the interaction of the given particle with the rest of the gas is
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \langle h_{\mathrm {pot} }\rangle =\int _{0}^{\infty }4\pi r^{2}\rho U(r)g(r)\,dr.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟨
               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                h
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  o
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟩
               <!-- ⟩ -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msubsup>
               <mo>
                ∫
                <!-- ∫ -->
               </mo>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 0
                </mn>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 ∞
                 <!-- ∞ -->
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msubsup>
              <mn>
               4
              </mn>
              <mi>
               π
               <!-- π -->
              </mi>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                r
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mi>
               U
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mi>
               r
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mi>
               g
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mi>
               r
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mi>
               d
              </mi>
              <mi>
               r
              </mi>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \langle h_{\mathrm {pot} }\rangle =\int _{0}^{\infty }4\pi r^{2}\rho U(r)g(r)\,dr.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\langle h_{{{\mathrm  {pot}}}}\rangle =\int _{{0}}^{{\infty }}4\pi r^{{2}}\rho U(r)g(r)\,dr." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bbd8ca8c03292686243d097751c6e02c7bcfa518" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:31.293ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       The total mean potential energy of the gas is therefore
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \langle H_{pot}\rangle ={\tfrac {1}{2}}N\langle h_{\mathrm {pot} }\rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              ⟨
              <!-- ⟨ -->
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               H
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
               <mi>

               </mi>
               <mi>

               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">

              <!-- ⟩ -->
             </mo>
             <mo>
              =
             </mo>
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">
               <mfrac>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mfrac>
              </mstyle>
             </mrow>
             <mi>
              N
             </mi>
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              ⟨
              <!-- ⟨ -->
             </mo>
             <msub>
              <mi>
               h
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 p
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 o
                </mi>
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 t
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
             </msub>
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              ⟩
              <!-- ⟩ -->
             </mo>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \langle H_{pot}\rangle ={\tfrac {1}{2}}N\langle h_{\mathrm {pot} }\rangle }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\langle H_{{pot}}\rangle ={\tfrac  12}N\langle h_{{{\mathrm  {pot}}}}\rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/124d357e70d0da6034201abd438cecdc718345ee" style="vertical-align: -1.171ex; width:18.767ex; height:3.509ex;"/>
       </span>
       , where
       <i>
        N
       </i>
       is the number of particles in the gas, and the factor ​
       <span class="frac nowrap">
        <sup>
         1
        </sup>
        ⁄
        <sub>
         2
        </sub>
       </span>
       is needed because summation over all the particles counts each interaction twice. Adding kinetic and potential energies, then applying equipartition, yields the
       <i>
        energy equation
       </i>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">

            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="H=\langle H_{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}\rangle +\langle H_{{{\mathrm  {pot}}}}\rangle ={\frac  {3}{2}}Nk_{{B}}T+2\pi N\rho \int _{{0}}^{{\infty }}r^{{2}}U(r)g(r)\,dr." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a570a4e9ebebdb6a24e891e6100f8f7296b07ffe" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:59.781ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       A similar argument,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       can be used to derive the
       <i>
        pressure equation
       </i>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
