      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Anharmonic_oscillators">
        Anharmonic oscillators
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Anharmonic oscillators">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Anharmonic_oscillator" title="Anharmonic oscillator">
        Anharmonic oscillator
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       An anharmonic oscillator (in contrast to a simple harmonic oscillator) is one in which the potential energy is not quadratic in the extension
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       (the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Canonical_coordinate" title="Canonical coordinate">
        generalized position
       </a>
       which measures the deviation of the system from equilibrium). Such oscillators provide a complementary point of view on the equipartition theorem.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tolman_1927_37-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-tolman_1927-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-terletskii_1971_38-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-terletskii_1971-38">
         [38]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Simple examples are provided by potential energy functions of the form
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {pot} }=Cq^{s},\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                H
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  o
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 s
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {pot} }=Cq^{s},\,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="H_{{{\mathrm  {pot}}}}=Cq^{{s}},\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c9e1d9280a68aef4b3266c17fcdbb7d7dd5da69c" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:12.521ex; height:3.009ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <i>
        C
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        s
       </i>
       are arbitrary
       <a href="/wiki/Real_number" title="Real number">
        real constants
       </a>
       . In these cases, the law of equipartition predicts that
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle k_{\rm {B}}T={\Bigl \langle }q{\frac {\partial H_{\mathrm {pot} }}{\partial q}}{\Bigr \rangle }=\langle q\cdot sCq^{s-1}\rangle =\langle sCq^{s}\rangle =s\langle H_{\mathrm {pot} }\rangle .}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  B
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   H
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     p
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     o
                    </mi>
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     t
                    </mi>
                   </mrow>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  q
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟨
               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               q
              </mi>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               s
              </mi>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 s
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟩
               <!-- ⟩ -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟨
               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>
              <mi>
               s
              </mi>
              <mi>
               C
              </mi>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 s
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟩
               <!-- ⟩ -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mi>
               s
              </mi>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟨
               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                H
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  o
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟩
               <!-- ⟩ -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle k_{\rm {B}}T={\Bigl \langle }q{\frac {\partial H_{\mathrm {pot} }}{\partial q}}{\Bigr \rangle }=\langle q\cdot sCq^{s-1}\rangle =\langle sCq^{s}\rangle =s\langle H_{\mathrm {pot} }\rangle .}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="k_{{{\rm {B}}}}T={\Bigl \langle }q{\frac  {\partial H_{{{\mathrm  {pot}}}}}{\partial q}}{\Bigr \rangle }=\langle q\cdot sCq^{{s-1}}\rangle =\langle sCq^{{s}}\rangle =s\langle H_{{{\mathrm  {pot}}}}\rangle ." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b2c1d67755a4b9aa03ebeb0cd613d276cb2901b0" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:53.673ex; height:6.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Thus, the average potential energy equals
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       /
       <i>
        s
       </i>
       , not
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       /2 as for the quadratic harmonic oscillator (where
       <i>
        s
       </i>
       = 2).
      </p>
      <p>
       More generally, a typical energy function of a one-dimensional system has a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taylor_expansion" title="Taylor expansion">
        Taylor expansion
       </a>
       in the extension
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       :
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {pot} }=\sum _{n=2}^{\infty }C_{n}q^{n}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                H
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  p
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  o
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <munderover>
               <mo>
                ∑
                <!-- ∑ -->
               </mo>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 =
                </mo>
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="normal">
                 ∞
                 <!-- ∞ -->
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </munderover>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                C
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 n
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {pot} }=\sum _{n=2}^{\infty }C_{n}q^{n}}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="H_{{{\mathrm  {pot}}}}=\sum _{{n=2}}^{{\infty }}C_{{n}}q^{{n}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6bee61138b8574b1fcfa6cbb5024cbfc7e0f6ff5" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:16.558ex; height:6.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       for non-negative
       <a href="/wiki/Integer" title="Integer">
        integers
       </a>
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       . There is no
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       = 1 term, because at the equilibrium point, there is no net force and so the first derivative of the energy is zero. The
       <i>
        n
       </i>
       = 0 term need not be included, since the energy at the equilibrium position may be set to zero by convention. In this case, the law of equipartition predicts that
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tolman_1927_37-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-tolman_1927-37">
         [37]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <dl>

      <p>
       In contrast to the other examples cited here, the equipartition formula

      <p>
       does
       <i>
        not
       </i>
       allow the average potential energy to be written in terms of known constants.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Brownian_motion">
        Brownian motion
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Brownian motion">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:402px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Wiener_process_3d.png">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="883" data-file-width="904" height="391" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Wiener_process_3d.png/400px-Wiener_process_3d.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Wiener_process_3d.png/600px-Wiener_process_3d.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f8/Wiener_process_3d.png/800px-Wiener_process_3d.png 2x" width="400"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Wiener_process_3d.png" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Figure 7. Typical Brownian motion of a particle in three dimensions.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">
        Brownian motion
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The equipartition theorem can be used to derive the
       <a href="/wiki/Brownian_motion" title="Brownian motion">
        Brownian motion
       </a>
       of a particle from the
       <a href="/wiki/Langevin_equation" title="Langevin equation">
        Langevin equation
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       According to that equation, the motion of a particle of mass
       <i>
        m
       </i>
       with velocity
       <b>
        v
       </b>
       is governed by
       <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_laws_of_motion" title="Newton's laws of motion">
        Newton's second law
       </a>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {d\mathbf {v} }{dt}}={\frac {1}{m}}\mathbf {F} =-{\frac {\mathbf {v} }{\tau }}+{\frac {1}{m}}\mathbf {F} _{\mathrm {rnd} },}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi mathvariant="bold">
                   v
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                F
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  v
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mi>
                 τ
                 <!-- τ -->
                </mi>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <msub>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi mathvariant="bold">
                 F
                </mi>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  r
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  n
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  d
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\frac {d\mathbf {v} }{dt}}={\frac {1}{m}}\mathbf {F} =-{\frac {\mathbf {v} }{\tau }}+{\frac {1}{m}}\mathbf {F} _{\mathrm {rnd} },}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\frac  {d{\mathbf  {v}}}{dt}}={\frac  {1}{m}}{\mathbf  {F}}=-{\frac  {{\mathbf  {v}}}{\tau }}+{\frac  {1}{m}}{\mathbf  {F}}_{{{\mathrm  {rnd}}}}," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/63b698f245197aa236121978bd6bc02073c6542e" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:29.026ex; height:5.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       <sub>
        rnd
       </sub>
       is a random force representing the random collisions of the particle and the surrounding molecules, and where the
       <a href="/wiki/Time_constant" title="Time constant">
        time constant
       </a>
       τ reflects the
       <a href="/wiki/Drag_(physics)" title="Drag (physics)">
        drag force
       </a>
       that opposes the particle's motion through the solution. The drag force is often written
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       <sub>
        drag
       </sub>
       = −γ
       <b>
        v
       </b>
       ; therefore, the time constant τ equals
       <i>
        m
       </i>
       /γ.
      </p>
      <p>
       The dot product of this equation with the position vector
       <b>
        r
       </b>
       , after averaging, yields the equation
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }\mathbf {r} \cdot {\frac {d\mathbf {v} }{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle }+{\frac {1}{\tau }}\langle \mathbf {r} \cdot \mathbf {v} \rangle =0}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-OPEN">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟨
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                r
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                  <mi mathvariant="bold">
                   v
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 ⟩
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               +
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mn>
                 1
                </mn>
                <mi>
                 τ
                 <!-- τ -->
                </mi>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟨
               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                r
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ⋅
               <!-- ⋅ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi mathvariant="bold">
                v
               </mi>
              </mrow>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟩
               <!-- ⟩ -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               0
              </mn>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\Bigl \langle }\mathbf {r} \cdot {\frac {d\mathbf {v} }{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle }+{\frac {1}{\tau }}\langle \mathbf {r} \cdot \mathbf {v} \rangle =0}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\Bigl \langle }{\mathbf  {r}}\cdot {\frac  {d{\mathbf  {v}}}{dt}}{\Bigr \rangle }+{\frac  {1}{\tau }}\langle {\mathbf  {r}}\cdot {\mathbf  {v}}\rangle =0" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/19477f6c2cab46743a2914f53c8ade51774765e4" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:24.226ex; height:5.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       for Brownian motion (since the random force
       <b>
        F
       </b>
       <sub>
        rnd
       </sub>
       is uncorrelated with the position
       <b>
        r
       </b>
       ). Using the mathematical identities
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {d}{dt}}\left(\mathbf {r} \cdot \mathbf {r} \right)={\frac {d}{dt}}\left(r^{2}\right)=2\left(\mathbf {r} \cdot \mathbf {v} \right)}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mi>
                 d
                </mi>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  r
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 ⋅
                 <!-- ⋅ -->
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  r
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mi>
                 d
                </mi>
                <mrow>
                 <mi>
                  d
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <msup>
                <mi>
                 r
                </mi>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mn>
                  2
                 </mn>
                </mrow>
               </msup>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               2
              </mn>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  r
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 ⋅
                 <!-- ⋅ -->
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="bold">
                  v
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">

                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mi>
                 m
                </mi>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               t
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  6
                 </mn>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   k
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mi>
                    B
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                 <mi>
                  T
                 </mi>
                 <mi>
                  t
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mi>
                 γ
                 <!-- γ -->
                </mi>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \langle r^{2}\rangle \approx {\frac {6k_{B}T\tau }{m}}t={\frac {6k_{B}Tt}{\gamma }}.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\langle r^{{2}}\rangle \approx {\frac  {6k_{{B}}T\tau }{m}}t={\frac  {6k_{{B}}Tt}{\gamma }}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f9382775fa76f5f86cd6256a259730e24c2e2ced" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:26.288ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       This describes the
       <a href="/wiki/Diffusion" title="Diffusion">
        diffusion
       </a>
       of the particle over time. An analogous equation for the rotational diffusion of a rigid molecule can be derived in a similar way.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Stellar_physics">
        Stellar physics
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Stellar physics">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       See also:
       <a href="/wiki/Astrophysics" title="Astrophysics">
        Astrophysics
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Stellar_structure" title="Stellar structure">
        Stellar structure
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The equipartition theorem and the related
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_theorem" title="Virial theorem">
        virial theorem
       </a>
       have long been used as a tool in
       <a href="/wiki/Astrophysics" title="Astrophysics">
        astrophysics
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39">
        <a href="#cite_note-39">
         [39]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As examples, the virial theorem may be used to estimate stellar temperatures or the
       <a href="/wiki/Chandrasekhar_limit" title="Chandrasekhar limit">
        Chandrasekhar limit
       </a>
       on the mass of
       <a href="/wiki/White_dwarf" title="White dwarf">
        white dwarf
       </a>
       stars.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         [40]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         [41]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The average temperature of a star can be estimated from the equipartition theorem.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         [42]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Since most stars are spherically symmetric, the total
       <a href="/wiki/Newton%27s_law_of_universal_gravitation" title="Newton's law of universal gravitation">
        gravitational
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Potential_energy#Gravitational_potential_energy" title="Potential energy">
        potential energy
       </a>
       can be estimated by integration
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {grav} }=-\int _{0}^{R}{\frac {4\pi r^{2}G}{r}}M(r)\,\rho (r)\,dr,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msub>
               <mi>
                H
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  g
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  r
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  a
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  v
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo>
               −
               <!-- − -->
              </mo>
              <msubsup>
               <mo>
                ∫
                <!-- ∫ -->
               </mo>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 0
                </mn>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 R
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msubsup>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  4
                 </mn>
                 <mi>
                  π
                  <!-- π -->
                 </mi>
                 <msup>
                  <mi>
                   r
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mn>
                    2
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msup>
                 <mi>
                  G
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
                <mi>
                 r
                </mi>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               M
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mi>
               r
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mi>

              </mo>

            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle H_{\mathrm {grav} }=-\int _{0}^{R}{\frac {4\pi r^{2}G}{r}}M(r)\,\rho (r)\,dr,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="H_{{{\mathrm  {grav}}}}=-\int _{0}^{R}{\frac  {4\pi r^{2}G}{r}}M(r)\,\rho (r)\,dr," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/09575b27b0bba70237e2c215e39abe9540a6fd29" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:35.25ex; height:6.176ex;"/>
        </span>

       where
       <i>

       (
       <i>
        r

       <i>
        r

      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>

       where

       <i>

       , where
       <i>
        m

       </sub>
       is the mass of one proton. Application of the equipartition theorem gives an estimate of the star's temperature
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">

                  ∂
                  <!-- ∂ -->
                 </mi>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   H
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

         <img alt="{\Bigl \langle }r{\frac  {\partial H_{{{\mathrm  {grav}}}}}{\partial r}}{\Bigr \rangle }=\langle -H_{{{\mathrm  {grav}}}}\rangle =k_{B}T={\frac  {3GM^{2}}{5RN}}." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/aa9fd01ed193a9d634ebe59ffd069e66404de6cd" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:41.948ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Substitution of the mass and radius of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">
        Sun
       </a>
       yields an estimated solar temperature of
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       = 14 million kelvins, very close to its core temperature of 15 million kelvins. However, the Sun is much more complex than assumed by this model—both its temperature and density vary strongly with radius—and such excellent agreement (≈7%
       <a href="/wiki/Approximation_error" title="Approximation error">
        relative error
       </a>
       ) is partly fortuitous.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         [43]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Star_formation">
        Star formation
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Star formation">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The same formulae may be applied to determining the conditions for
       <a href="/wiki/Star_formation" title="Star formation">
        star formation
       </a>
       in giant
       <a href="/wiki/Molecular_cloud" title="Molecular cloud">
        molecular clouds
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         [44]
        </a>
       </sup>
       A local fluctuation in the density of such a cloud can lead to a runaway condition in which the cloud collapses inwards under its own gravity. Such a collapse occurs when the equipartition theorem—or, equivalently, the
       <a href="/wiki/Virial_theorem" title="Virial theorem">
        virial theorem
       </a>
       —is no longer valid, i.e., when the gravitational potential energy exceeds twice the kinetic energy
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\frac {3GM^{2}}{5R}}&gt;3Nk_{B}T.}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  3
                 </mn>
                 <mi>
                  G
                 </mi>
                 <msup>
                  <mi>
                   M
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mn>
                    2
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msup>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  5
                 </mn>
                 <mi>
                  R
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               &gt;
              </mo>
              <mn>
               3
              </mn>
              <mi>
               N
              </mi>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                k
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 B
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mi>
               T
              </mi>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\frac {3GM^{2}}{5R}}&gt;3Nk_{B}T.}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\frac  {3GM^{{2}}}{5R}}&gt;3Nk_{{B}}T." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/29dddd9801b530af78876d91800ea20da1aaf5a1" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:18.677ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Assuming a constant density ρ for the cloud
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle M={\frac {4}{3}}\pi R^{3}\rho }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               M
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mfrac>
                <mn>
                 4
                </mn>
                <mn>
                 3
                </mn>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               π
               <!-- π -->
              </mi>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                R
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 3
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle M={\frac {4}{3}}\pi R^{3}\rho }
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="M={\frac  {4}{3}}\pi R^{{3}}\rho " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4b2b4c920d251b6a77afe5a9ad4c0e15300bc5b1" style="vertical-align: -1.838ex; width:12.891ex; height:5.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       yields a minimum mass for stellar contraction, the Jeans mass
       <i>
        M
       </i>
       <sub>
        J
       </sub>
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle M_{\rm {J}}^{2}=\left({\frac {5k_{B}T}{Gm_{p}}}\right)^{3}\left({\frac {3}{4\pi \rho }}\right).}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <msubsup>
               <mi>
                M
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  J
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 2
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msubsup>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mrow>
                <mo>
                 (
                </mo>
                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                 <mfrac>
                  <mrow>
                   <mn>
                    5
                   </mn>
                   <msub>
                    <mi>
                     k
                    </mi>
                    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                     <mi>
                      B
                     </mi>
                    </mrow>
                   </msub>
                   <mi>
                    T
                   </mi>
                  </mrow>
                  <mrow>
                   <mi>
                    G
                   </mi>
                   <msub>
                    <mi>
                     m
                    </mi>
                    <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                     <mi>
                      p
                     </mi>
                    </mrow>
                   </msub>
                  </mrow>
                 </mfrac>
                </mrow>
                <mo>
                 )
                </mo>
               </mrow>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>
                 3
                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mrow>
               <mo>
                (
               </mo>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mfrac>
                 <mn>
                  3
                 </mn>
                 <mrow>
                  <mn>
                   4
                  </mn>
                  <mi>
                   π
                   <!-- π -->
                  </mi>
                  <mi>
                   ρ
                   <!-- ρ -->
                  </mi>
                 </mrow>
                </mfrac>
               </mrow>
               <mo>
                )
               </mo>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               .
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle M_{\rm {J}}^{2}=\left({\frac {5k_{B}T}{Gm_{p}}}\right)^{3}\left({\frac {3}{4\pi \rho }}\right).}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="M_{{{\rm {J}}}}^{{2}}=\left({\frac  {5k_{{B}}T}{Gm_{{p}}}}\right)^{{3}}\left({\frac  {3}{4\pi \rho }}\right)." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/14ffc68ea323d79de513833a6784f46758f8523b" style="vertical-align: -2.671ex; width:26.827ex; height:6.676ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Substituting the values typically observed in such clouds (
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       = 150 K, ρ = 2
       <span style="margin:0 .15em 0 .25em">
        ×
       </span>
       10
       <sup>
        −16
       </sup>
       g/cm
       <sup>
        3
       </sup>
       ) gives an estimated minimum mass of 17 solar masses, which is consistent with observed star formation. This effect is also known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Jeans_instability" title="Jeans instability">
        Jeans instability
       </a>
       , after the British physicist
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/James_Hopwood_Jeans" title="James Hopwood Jeans">
        James Hopwood Jeans
       </a>
       who published it in 1902.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         [45]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Derivations">
        Derivations
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Derivations">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span id="Kinetic_energies_and_the_Maxwell.E2.80.93Boltzmann_distribution">
       </span>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Kinetic_energies_and_the_Maxwell–Boltzmann_distribution">
        Kinetic energies and the Maxwell–Boltzmann distribution
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Kinetic energies and the Maxwell–Boltzmann distribution">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The original formulation of the equipartition theorem states that, in any physical system in
       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_equilibrium" title="Thermal equilibrium">
        thermal equilibrium
       </a>
       , every particle has exactly the same average
       <a href="/wiki/Kinetic_energy" title="Kinetic energy">
        kinetic energy
       </a>
       , (3/2)
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcquarrie_2000a_46-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mcquarrie_2000a-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This may be shown using the
       <a href="/wiki/Maxwell%E2%80%93Boltzmann_distribution" title="Maxwell–Boltzmann distribution">
        Maxwell–Boltzmann distribution
       </a>
       (see Figure 2), which is the probability distribution
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle f(v)=4\pi \left({\frac {m}{2\pi k_{\rm {B}}T}}\right)^{3/2}\!\!v^{2}\exp {\Bigl (}{\frac {-mv^{2}}{2k_{\rm {B}}T}}{\Bigr )}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>

               )
              </mo>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               4
              </mn>
              <mi>
               π
               <!-- π -->
              </mi>

                 </mo>

                </mn>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mspace width="negativethinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                v
               </mi>

               </mrow>

              </mi>
              <mo>

               <!-- ⁡ -->
              </mo>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                </mo>
               </mrow>

                  −
                  <!-- − -->
                 </mo>
                 <mi>
                  m
                 </mi>
                 <msup>
                  <mi>
                   v
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mn>
                    2
                   </mn>
                  </mrow>
                 </msup>
                </mrow>
                <mrow>
                 <mn>
                  2
                 </mn>
                 <msub>
                  <mi>
                   k
                  </mi>
                  <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                    <mi mathvariant="normal">
                     B
                    </mi>
                   </mrow>
                  </mrow>
                 </msub>
                 <mi>
                  T
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mfrac>
              </mrow>
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-CLOSE">
                <mo maxsize="1.623em" minsize="1.623em">
                 )
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle f(v)=4\pi \left({\frac {m}{2\pi k_{\rm {B}}T}}\right)^{3/2}\!\!v^{2}\exp {\Bigl (}{\frac {-mv^{2}}{2k_{\rm {B}}T}}{\Bigr )}}
            </annotation>

          </math>
         </span>

       for the speed of a particle of mass

       </a>

             </mo>

           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \mathbf {v} =(v_{x},v_{y},v_{z}).}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="{\mathbf  {v}}=(v_{x},v_{y},v_{z})." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/3f7aad02e8fe46976f687e1d53e69a76cb720e50" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:15.64ex; height:3.009ex;"/>
       </span>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Maxwell–Boltzmann distribution applies to any system composed of atoms, and assumes only a
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_ensemble" title="Canonical ensemble">
        canonical ensemble
       </a>
       , specifically, that the kinetic energies are distributed according to their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boltzmann_factor" title="Boltzmann factor">
        Boltzmann factor
       </a>
       at a temperature
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mcquarrie_2000a_46-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mcquarrie_2000a-46">
         [46]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The average kinetic energy for a particle of mass
       <i>
        m
       </i>
       is then given by the integral formula
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle \langle H_{\mathrm {kin} }\rangle =\langle {\tfrac {1}{2}}mv^{2}\rangle =\int _{0}^{\infty }{\tfrac {1}{2}}mv^{2}\ f(v)\ dv={\tfrac {3}{2}}k_{\rm {B}}T,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">

               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>

               </mi>

                  k
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  i
                 </mi>
                 <mi mathvariant="normal">
                  n
                 </mi>
                </mrow>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟩
               <!-- ⟩ -->
              </mo>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
               ⟨
               <!-- ⟨ -->
              </mo>

               <mstyle displaystyle="false" scriptlevel="0">

                  1
                 </mn>
                 <mn>
                  2

                </mfrac>
               </mstyle>
              </mrow>
              <mi>
               m
              </mi>
              <msup>

              </mo>

              </mo>

               </mo>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mn>

                </mn>
               </mrow>

                 ∞
                 <!-- ∞ -->
                </mi>
               </mrow>

              </mi>

               (
              </mo>
              <mi>

               )
              </mo>
              <mtext>
              </mtext>
              <mi>
               d
              </mi>

              </mi>

              </mo>

                  2
                 </mn>

              </mrow>

                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">

                 </mi>

               </mrow>
              </msub>

            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="\langle H_{{{\mathrm  {kin}}}}\rangle =\langle {\tfrac  {1}{2}}mv^{{2}}\rangle =\int _{{0}}^{{\infty }}{\tfrac  {1}{2}}mv^{{2}}\ f(v)\ dv={\tfrac  {3}{2}}k_{{{\rm {B}}}}T," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/d5a1a90ee243385fcaeac7030d98c2c15befdd7e" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:48.073ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       as stated by the equipartition theorem. The same result can also be obtained by averaging the particle energy using the probability of finding the particle in certain quantum energy state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-configint_35-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-configint-35">
         [35]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Quadratic_energies_and_the_partition_function">
        Quadratic energies and the partition function
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Quadratic energies and the partition function">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       More generally, the equipartition theorem states that any
       <a href="/wiki/Degrees_of_freedom_(physics_and_chemistry)" title="Degrees of freedom (physics and chemistry)">
        degree of freedom
       </a>
       <i>
        x
       </i>
       which appears in the total energy
       <i>
        H
       </i>
       only as a simple quadratic term
       <i>
        Ax
       </i>
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       , where
       <i>
        A
       </i>
       is a constant, has an average energy of ½
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       in thermal equilibrium. In this case the equipartition theorem may be derived from the
       <a href="/wiki/Partition_function_(statistical_mechanics)" title="Partition function (statistical mechanics)">
        partition function
       </a>
       <i>
        Z
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        β
       </i>
       ), where
       <i>
        β
       </i>
       = 1/(
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       ) is the canonical
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inverse_temperature" title="Inverse temperature">
        inverse temperature
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         [47]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Integration over the variable
       <i>
        x
       </i>
       yields a factor
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>

      <p>
       in the formula for
       <i>

      <p>
       as stated by the equipartition theorem.
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="General_proofs">
        General proofs
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: General proofs">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       General derivations of the equipartition theorem can be found in many
       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">
        statistical mechanics
       </a>
       textbooks, both for the
       <a href="/wiki/Microcanonical_ensemble" title="Microcanonical ensemble">
        microcanonical ensemble
       </a>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huang_1987_9-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-huang_1987-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and for the
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_ensemble" title="Canonical ensemble">
        canonical ensemble
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tolman_1938_33-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-tolman_1938-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       They involve taking averages over the
       <a href="/wiki/Phase_space" title="Phase space">
        phase space
       </a>
       of the system, which is a
       <a href="/wiki/Symplectic_manifold" title="Symplectic manifold">
        symplectic manifold
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       To explain these derivations, the following notation is introduced. First, the phase space is described in terms of
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_coordinates" title="Canonical coordinates">
        generalized position coordinates
       </a>
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       <sub>
        <i>
         j
        </i>
       </sub>
       together with their
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Conjugate_momentum" title="Conjugate momentum">
        conjugate momenta
       </a>
       <i>
        p
       </i>
       <sub>
        <i>
         j
        </i>
       </sub>
       . The quantities
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       <sub>
        <i>
         j
        </i>
       </sub>
       completely describe the
       <a href="/wiki/Configuration_space_(physics)" title="Configuration space (physics)">
        configuration
       </a>
       of the system, while the quantities (
       <i>
        q
       </i>
       <sub>
        <i>
         j
        </i>
       </sub>
       ,
       <i>
        p
       </i>
       <sub>
        <i>
         j
        </i>
       </sub>
       ) together completely describe its
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_mechanics" title="Classical mechanics">
        state
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <p>
       Secondly, the infinitesimal volume
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle d\Gamma =\prod _{i}dq_{i}\,dp_{i}\,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mi>
               d
              </mi>
              <mi mathvariant="normal">
               Γ
               <!-- Γ -->
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <munder>
               <mo>
                ∏
                <!-- ∏ -->
               </mo>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 i
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </munder>
              <mi>
               d
              </mi>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                q
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 i
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
              <mi>
               d
              </mi>
              <msub>
               <mi>
                p
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi>
                 i
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </msub>
              <mspace width="thinmathspace">
              </mspace>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle d\Gamma =\prod _{i}dq_{i}\,dp_{i}\,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="d\Gamma =\prod _{i}dq_{i}\,dp_{i}\," aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e8727c2f215e5e314487d84f6c0b47e6b6680970" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:16.135ex; height:5.509ex;"/>
        </span>

      <p>
       of the phase space is introduced and used to define the volume Σ(
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       , Δ
       <i>

       </i>
       ) of the portion of phase space where the energy
       <i>

       </i>

       <i>

       </i>
       and
       <i>

       </i>

      </p>

              </mo>
              <mi mathvariant="normal">
               Δ
               <!-- Δ -->
              </mi>
              <mi>
               E
              </mi>
              <mtext>
              </mtext>
              <mi>
               ρ
               <!-- ρ -->
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               (
              </mo>
              <mi>
               E
              </mi>
              <mo stretchy="false">
               )
              </mo>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle \Sigma =\Delta E\ {\frac {\partial \Omega }{\partial E}}=\Delta E\ \rho (E),}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\displaystyle \Sigma =\Delta E\ {\frac {\partial \Omega }{\partial E}}=\Delta E\ \rho (E),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/76bb0f2eded1601fabe2f5a62bb183a590fe5a25" style="vertical-align: -2.005ex; width:25.823ex; height:5.509ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <i>

       (
       <i>

       ) is the
       <a href="/wiki/Density_of_states" title="Density of states">

       </a>

       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">

       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Entropy" title="Entropy">
        entropy
       </a>
       <i>

       </i>
       equals
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       log
       <i>
        Ω
       </i>
       (
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       ), and the
       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">
        temperature
       </a>
       <i>

       </i>
       is defined by
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">

      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_canonical_ensemble">
        The canonical ensemble
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: The canonical ensemble">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In the
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_ensemble" title="Canonical ensemble">
        canonical ensemble
       </a>
       , the system is in
       <a href="/wiki/Thermal_equilibrium" title="Thermal equilibrium">
        thermal equilibrium
       </a>
       with an infinite heat bath at
       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">
        temperature
       </a>
       <i>
        T
       </i>
       (in kelvins).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pathria_1972_5-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-pathria_1972-5">
         [5]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tolman_1938_33-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-tolman_1938-33">
         [33]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The probability of each state in
       <a href="/wiki/Phase_space" title="Phase space">
        phase space
       </a>
       is given by its
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boltzmann_factor" title="Boltzmann factor">
        Boltzmann factor
       </a>
       times a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Normalization_factor" title="Normalization factor">
        normalization factor
       </a>
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\mathcal {N}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mi class="MJX-tex-caligraphic" mathvariant="script">
                N
               </mi>
              </mrow>
             </mrow>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle {\mathcal {N}}}
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="{\mathcal {N}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b7551c7bed2cd2ee83e10536d157c94a5f8f72fd" style="vertical-align: -0.338ex; margin-left: -0.062ex; width:2.337ex; height:2.509ex;"/>
       </span>
       , which is chosen so that the probabilities sum to one
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\mathcal {N}}\int e^{-\beta H(p,q)}d\Gamma =1,}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
           <semantics>
            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mi class="MJX-tex-caligraphic" mathvariant="script">
                 N
                </mi>
               </mrow>
              </mrow>
              <mo>
               ∫
               <!-- ∫ -->
              </mo>
              <msup>
               <mi>
                e
               </mi>
               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
                <mo>
                 −
                 <!-- − -->
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 β
                 <!-- β -->
                </mi>
                <mi>
                 H
                </mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 (
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 p
                </mi>
                <mo>
                 ,
                </mo>
                <mi>
                 q
                </mi>
                <mo stretchy="false">
                 )
                </mo>
               </mrow>
              </msup>
              <mi>
               d
              </mi>
              <mi mathvariant="normal">
               Γ
               <!-- Γ -->
              </mi>
              <mo>
               =
              </mo>
              <mn>
               1
              </mn>
              <mo>
               ,
              </mo>
             </mstyle>
            </mrow>
            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
             {\displaystyle {\mathcal {N}}\int e^{-\beta H(p,q)}d\Gamma =1,}
            </annotation>
           </semantics>
          </math>

        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       where
       <i>
        β
       </i>
       = 1/
       <i>
        k
       </i>
       <sub>
        B
       </sub>
       <i>

       <a href="/wiki/Integration_by_parts" title="Integration by parts">
        Integration by parts
       </a>

       <i>

           </semantics>
          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\mathcal  {N}}\int e^{{-\beta H(p,q)}}x_{{k}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial x_{{k}}}}\,d\Gamma ={\Bigl \langle }x_{{k}}{\frac  {\partial H}{\partial x_{{k}}}}{\Bigr \rangle }={\frac  {1}{\beta }}=k_{{B}}T." aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a5b21ddf3f4318e836b367664de096f60ceaf4c6" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; margin-left: -0.062ex; width:49.935ex; height:5.843ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       Here, the averaging symbolized by
       <span class="mwe-math-element">
        <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
         <math alttext="{\displaystyle \langle \ldots \rangle }" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">
          <semantics>
           <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">
            <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              ⟨
              <!-- ⟨ -->
             </mo>
             <mo>
              …
              <!-- … -->
             </mo>
             <mo fence="false" stretchy="false">
              ⟩
              <!-- ⟩ -->
             </mo>
            </mstyle>
           </mrow>
           <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">
            {\displaystyle \langle \ldots \rangle }
           </annotation>
          </semantics>
         </math>
        </span>
        <img alt="\langle \ldots \rangle " aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/f8f365afc3303fd926e94a51545a0d72d54a2eb5" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:4.533ex; height:2.843ex;"/>
       </span>
       is the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ensemble_average" title="Ensemble average">
        ensemble average
       </a>
       taken over the
       <a href="/wiki/Canonical_ensemble" title="Canonical ensemble">
        canonical ensemble
       </a>
       .
      </p>
      <h4>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="The_microcanonical_ensemble">
        The microcanonical ensemble
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Equipartition_theorem&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: The microcanonical ensemble">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h4>
      <p>
       In the microcanonical ensemble, the system is isolated from the rest of the world, or at least very weakly coupled to it.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-huang_1987_9-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-huang_1987-9">
         [9]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Hence, its total energy is effectively constant; to be definite, we say that the total energy
       <i>
        H
       </i>
       is confined between
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       +d
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       . For a given energy
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       and spread d
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       , there is a region of
       <a href="/wiki/Phase_space" title="Phase space">
        phase space
       </a>
       Σ in which the system has that energy, and the probability of each state in that region of
       <a href="/wiki/Phase_space" title="Phase space">
        phase space
       </a>
       is equal, by the definition of the microcanonical ensemble. Given these definitions, the equipartition average of phase-space variables
       <i>
        x
        <sub>
         m
        </sub>
       </i>
       (which could be either
       <i>
        q
        <sub>
         k
        </sub>
       </i>
       or
       <i>
        p
        <sub>
         k
        </sub>
       </i>
       ) and
       <i>
        x
        <sub>
         n
        </sub>
       </i>
       is given by
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">
          <math alttext="{\displaystyle {\begin{aligned}{\Bigl \langle }x_{m}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}{\Bigr \rangle }&amp;={\frac {1}{\Sigma }}\,\int _{H\in \left[E,E+\Delta E\right]}x_{m}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}\,d\Gamma \\&amp;={\frac {\Delta E}{\Sigma }}\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial E}}\int _{H&lt;E}x_{m}{\frac {\partial H}{\partial x_{n}}}\,d\Gamma \\&amp;={\frac {1}{\rho }}\,{\frac {\partial }{\partial E}}\int _{H&lt;E}x_{m}{\frac {\partial \left(H-E\right)}{\partial x_{n}}}\,d\Gamma ,\end{aligned}}}" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">

          </math>
         </span>
         <img alt="{\begin{aligned}\int _{{H&lt;E}}x_{{m}}{\frac  {\partial (H-E)}{\partial x_{{n}}}}\,d\Gamma &amp;=\int _{{H&lt;E}}{\frac  {\partial }{\partial x_{{n}}}}{\bigl (}x_{{m}}(H-E){\bigr )}\,d\Gamma -\int _{{H&lt;E}}\delta _{{mn}}(H-E)d\Gamma \\&amp;=\delta _{{mn}}\int _{{H&lt;E}}(E-H)\,d\Gamma ,\end{aligned}}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/801cfe2696ae376a32f3dd8fe04fcd7bc7741cab" style="vertical-align: -5.505ex; width:77.342ex; height:12.176ex;"/>
        </span>
       </dd>
      </dl>
      <p>
       since the first term on the right hand side of the first line is zero (it can be rewritten as an integral of
       <i>
        H
       </i>
       −
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       on the
       <a href="/wiki/Hypersurface" title="Hypersurface">
        hypersurface
       </a>
       where
       <i>
        H
       </i>
       =
       <i>
        E
       </i>
       ).
      </p>
      <p>
       Substitution of this result into the previous equation yields
      </p>
      <dl>
       <dd>
        <span class="mwe-math-element">
